Saito in a Dilemma 60

Takahashi's Resignation Intent is Firm and Cannot be Persuaded to Stay

The Prime Minister Will Visit the Genro Again to Seek Understanding

The Current Cabinet's Life May Not Exceed May

(Tokyo) Prime Minister Saito met with Finance Minister Takahashi at the Prime Minister's residence at 9:35 this morning. The two elderly men held a secret discussion about the future of the Japanese political situation for a long time. It is said that Takahashi's intention to resign is very firm and the Prime Minister cannot persuade him to stay. At 10:50, the Prime Minister met with Justice Minister Oyama again. Although Saito tried his best to persuade him to stay temporarily, Oyama replied that the May 15 Incident was closely related to the red judicial officers and that he could not help but resign to take responsibility. As a result, the Prime Minister's meeting with the two ministers was extremely pessimistic. It is said that Saito, realizing the darkness of the future, plans to rush to Okitsu to revisit Genro Saionji after the emergency cabinet meeting closes, requesting the Genro's understanding. General observations are that the Prime Minister's revisit to the Genro is mostly preparing for the procedure of stepping down, and this trip is even more noteworthy. (4th China United Telegraph Dispatch)

It is Not Yet Time for the Entire Cabinet to Step Down 61

(Tokyo) After today's emergency cabinet meeting, Prime Minister Saito contacted Finance Minister Takahashi and Justice Minister Oyama again. The Prime Minister told Takahashi that although the budget had been approved, the specific implementation methods were not yet complete. If he wanted to step down, he would have to wait until after the results of the local governors' meeting to be held on the 17th before he could hand over responsibility. He expressed the same to Justice Minister Oyama, saying that the preliminary hearing of the May 15 Incident would soon be completed and that the charges against the red judicial officer case would soon be clarified. If Justice Minister Oyama could wait until the conclusion of the case, Saito would share responsibility with Oyama. In any case, each cabinet member must automatically dismiss the intention to resign in mid-April. In May, after various key domestic and foreign affairs have reached their respective "stages," they can discuss the issue of advance and retreat again. According to reports from the cabinet, Takahashi and Oyama have slightly accepted Saito's difficulties, and both have expressed their consent. (4th China United Telegraph Dispatch)

Seiyukai Expecting Political Change 62

(Tokyo) Seiyukai President Suzuki Kisaburo, who went to Yugawara Hot Spring to recuperate after the closure of the 64th Diet, suddenly received an emergency telegram from the Tokyo headquarters at 4:34 PM today, urging him to return to Tokyo. With the issue of Finance Minister Takahashi's resignation shelved, the actions of President Suzuki are particularly noteworthy. General speculation is that Suzuki intends to rush back to Tokyo to instigate a political change to be realized as soon as possible. (4th China United Telegraph Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Under the certainty that a political change is approaching, the Seiyukai is paying close attention to the political situation after Prime Minister Saito's visit to Genro. The Finance Minister's intention to resign is firm, and although the Prime Minister has repeatedly tried to persuade him to stay, he has not agreed. Furthermore, Justice Minister Oyama resigned to take responsibility due to ideological issues. In addition, the responsibility issues of Minister of Education Hatoyama and Minister of the Interior Yamamoto will ultimately be the responsibility of the Prime Minister. Therefore, the Seiyukai believes that supplementing and partially reforming cabinet members will not be able to muddle through for a while. As a result, the current cabinet will resign en masse at the end of this month or the beginning of next month. However, if the current cabinet does not resign even after May, the Seiyukai will withdraw cabinet members who are party members and decide to use the ultimate extraordinary means to collapse the cabinet. Therefore, even if it does not do this, the current cabinet will naturally collapse, saying that it is only a matter of time. (4th Electric Telegraph Dispatch)

Finance Minister Takahashi's Remarks 63

(Tokyo) Finance Minister Takahashi met with the Prime Minister before the cabinet meeting this morning. Saito earnestly persuaded Takahashi not to have the intention of resigning. Takahashi said that he was afraid that it would be difficult to agree to the Prime Minister's persuasion. After the meeting, Takahashi told Japanese reporters that whether he goes to war or not is a personal matter and is not convenient to disclose. He did have a private agreement with Yu Mu in the Diet. This is a private matter between the two and cannot be made public. He is physically weak and unable to bear the heavy responsibility again. He has recommended Vice Minister Kuroda to succeed him. Only the Seiyukai expects a political change due to his resignation. However, even if a political change follows, the people may not be able to fully trust the current political parties. It is not yet possible to determine who will be the successor cabinet. Moreover, since he is resigning for health reasons, it stands to reason that it should not affect the fate of the Saito cabinet. (4th China United Telegraph Dispatch)

European Four-Power Pact

France Prepares Counterproposal 71

Emphasizing Security More Than British and Italian Plans

Opposing Treaty Revision and Maintaining the Rights of Small Nations

Reuters, Paris, 3rd - After discussing the Four-Power Pact plan agreed upon by British Prime Minister MacDonald and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini in Rome, France will submit another plan. France is giving full consideration to the opposition of the three Little Entente countries of Czechoslovakia, Yugoslavia, and Romania to revising the treaty. After careful deliberation, the French cabinet has completed its draft statement, which emphasizes security more than the British and Italian plans. What it agrees with in the British and Italian plans is that the Four-Power Agreement should seek to resolve European problems through joint action, undertake not to increase armaments, and strive for an agreement on monetary issues. However, one matter that is very different from the original Italian proposal is the suggestion regarding treaty revision. France advocates that the signatory countries should comprehensively consider the Covenant of the League of Nations, so Article 19 of the Covenant must be handled in conjunction with Articles 3, 10, 11, and 16. Article 19 stipulates that the Assembly may reconsider treaties that are no longer applicable, while Articles 3 and 10 refer to events concerning world peace and the invasion of member states' territories. Therefore, France suggests that the undertaking of public safety should at least be given equal importance to the revision of treaties. The French do not regard this French draft as a counterproposal, but rather express the general principles in which France believes. The French draft also argues that whenever any issue arises involving any country other than the four powers, the countries concerned must always consult.

National News Agency, Paris, 3rd - The French cabinet decided tonight to send a note to Britain and Italy, stating that France in principle agrees with the Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's Four-Power Peace Pact proposal as a basis for discussion, but at the same time put forward some counterproposals and reservations to protect the Little Entente countries. The three Little Entente countries (according to the recent agreement, the three Little Entente countries have become a unit in international affairs) do not approve of modifying the treaty in a way that would increase the combined power of Germany and Italy, and especially oppose changing the borders of European countries as stipulated in the treaty at present. Therefore, France will solemnly declare in the note that the time is not yet ripe for any modifications to the treaty that would affect borders, but it is the long-cherished wish of the major powers to conclude an agreement to maintain and promote peace in Europe without infringing upon the rights of small countries. According to French diplomatic circles, there had previously been statements that France could accept the Four-Power Pact, but on the condition that small countries not be forced to join and comply.

Thunderstorms Strike, US Navy Airship Crashes into Sea 72

Only Four Rescued Out of Seventy-Seven Aboard

Airship Length 700 Feet, 4,000+ Horsepower

Cause of Accident Possibly Electrocution

Reuters, New York, 4th - The U.S. Navy airship Akron, the largest airship in the world, is reported to have crashed into the sea off the coast of New Jersey. There were a total of seventy-seven people on board. The airship is still floating near the Barnegat lightship. According to a report from the German oil tanker Forbes, several people have been rescued, but not all of them. The airship is 785 feet long, with a diameter of 132 feet 9 inches at its narrowest point. Its body is made of aluminum mixed with copper, making it light and strong, consisting of ten million individual parts, 54,000 fine struts, and 6.5 million rivets, weighing approximately 221,000 pounds. It is equipped with four engines on each side, totaling 4,480 horsepower, all installed internally, with only the eight propellers extending outwards. Its brakes are located at the bottom of the bow, and it can hold 6.5 million cubic feet of gas. Its top speed is 84 miles per hour, and it can fly 10,580 miles in one go.

Follow-up: According to a wireless telegram from the German oil tanker Forbes, the first officer and three crew members of the Akron airship have been rescued, and they are still moored nearby to rescue the remaining people.

Follow-up: Among those on board the Akron airship were Rear Admiral Moffett, Director of the Bureau of Aeronautics of the Navy Department, and several commanders of the Lakehurst Naval Air Station. In addition, there were 19 other officers. As of now, in addition to the four people rescued by the German oil tanker, there have been no further reports of survivors. Four coast guard vessels, a cruiser, a destroyer, and many other types of ships in the vicinity are rushing to the rescue. Washington has received a phone call from Lakehurst stating that the chances of survival for the remaining people are very slim. Due to poor weather conditions and poor visibility, reconnaissance aircraft cannot be dispatched to investigate. Although the Akron is still floating near the Barnegat lightship, it is feared that it has been completely destroyed. This morning, a wireless telegram was received here from the German ship Forbes stating that they are currently engaged in searching for survivors. Last night at 10:00 p.m., the Akron was still sending wireless telegrams, but due to thunderstorms, communication could not be continued.

Follow-up: According to the captain of the German ship Forbes, he saw an aircraft pass by in the thunderstorm, and then saw lights flashing on the water surface, and heard many people shouting for help. He immediately turned on all the lights on the ship and lowered the lifeboats to rescue the people, but only rescued three people, and witnessed the rest sinking before the lifeboats arrived. Judging from various signs, most of the people must have drowned.

National News Agency, New York, 3rd - The U.S. Navy airship Akron suddenly crashed into the ocean 22 miles outside the Barnegat Lighthouse tonight. Of the 19 officers and 57 soldiers on board, only three have been rescued so far, and only two have survived. Wireless operator Cobran died of serious injuries. It can truly be called the second major tragedy involving an American airship, and also the second incident since the Akron was completed. As for the cause of the disaster, it is still unknown. However, not long before the accident, at 1:04 a.m., the Lakehurst Navy Department office received the last telegram, stating that they were flying along the New England coast and everything was normal. Unexpectedly, at 2:30 a.m., a wireless message was received from the German oil tanker Forbes, reporting that the airship had crashed and was drifting on the ocean surface, and only three people had been rescued. They are currently patrolling the nearby waters. However, the Barnegat Lighthouse is in New Jersey, only 70 miles from New York. Navy Department personnel initially did not believe that the Akron could have crashed there. However, as telegrams from the Coast Guard and various shipping companies poured in, Navy Department personnel began to believe it. At that time, the Barnegat lifeboat station had already dispatched lifeboats to the scene of the accident. When the sky began to lighten, two Navy destroyers also arrived at the scene, and the lifeboat station also sent doctors and nurses to provide medical assistance. However, after the German ship discovered the ship, it encountered a major thunderstorm, greatly hindering rescue efforts. By the time it dawned, the airship had drifted 30 miles outside the lighthouse. The most famous of the missing personnel on board include the Director of the Bureau of Aeronautics, Moffett; the airship commander, Macgote; the commander of the Lakehurst airship station, Bray; and Bureau of Aeronautics member, Shet. This airship departed from Lakehurst on Sunday night, and unexpectedly encountered this tragic disaster. The United States has only built four large airships: the Shenandoah, the Los Angeles, the Akron, and the Macon. The Shenandoah was destroyed in a thunderstorm in 1925, and the Los Angeles was also decommissioned last year.

Reuters, Washington, 4th - The Navy Department reported to President Roosevelt today that the Akron airship encountered a storm and probably caught fire due to electrocution, resulting in the accident. The German oil tanker Forbes and two steamships are still searching for the missing crew members at the site of the Akron's accident.

Reuters, London, 3rd - Reuters learned tonight that the new bill against Russia that the British government intends to submit to the House of Commons authorizes the Minister of Commerce to issue orders to ban certain Russian goods or completely prohibit their import. US House of Representatives Passes Bill Prohibiting Disclosure of Diplomatic Secrets

National News Agency, Washington, 3rd - Today, the House of Representatives, at the request of the US President, passed a bill by a vote of 299 to 29 to prevent people from obtaining foreign secret codes, which would make it difficult for the government in diplomatic affairs. The bill prohibits people from publishing government secret documents that may harm national security and interests. Violators will be sentenced to imprisonment for up to ten years or fined $10,000. The introduction of this bill was completely unexpected even by the members of Congress, which can be said to be extremely abrupt. There is obviously a reason behind the scenes that it had to be passed quickly, but it was not explicitly stated. Afterwards, some people outside pointed out that this bill is tantamount to gagging the press. The State Department immediately issued a statement saying that this bill is to protect American diplomatic telegram codes and does not intend to silence the press or impose censorship.

Siamese King Issues Edict to Suppress Leftist Thought 76

Severe Penalties for Spreading Communism

Opening Up Gambling Ban to Increase Revenue

Reuters, Bangkok, 3rd - Today, the King of Siam issued an edict to eradicate communism in Siam. The edict stated that communism is sufficient to endanger the country. Hereafter, anyone who promotes communism shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to ten years or fined up to £450. Employees of communist societies shall also be subject to the same punishment, and members shall be subject to imprisonment for up to five years or fined £90. Bangkok is tranquil today, but foreign embassies are protected by troops to prevent disturbances. Reuters, Singapore, 4th - According to news from Bangkok, the Siamese authorities are now making every effort to increase national revenue. A man named Dai Dirong (transliteration), who previously made contributions to the Siamese government and was awarded a medal by the Siamese King, was very influential in the gambling industry before Siam banned gambling several years ago. Now, Dai has submitted a request to the Siamese government, willing to contract lotteries, reporting an annual contribution of approximately 5 million Siamese baht. This matter is currently under serious consideration by the Siamese authorities. When Dai was asked about this matter, he said that the government may entrust him with handling this lottery. Since the government has allowed gambling that is not beneficial to the country and the people, such as horse racing and card games, and the national treasury has been declining in the past three years, this gambling ban can be opened up to increase revenue. It is heard that lotteries are expected to be revived within this month, with a term of five years. Whether to continue after the term expires will be decided by the government.

(Enemy's General Offensive) Due to the failure of the Japanese Kwantung Army's attack on Xifengkou and Luowenyu, the Japanese High Command, in order to threaten the garrisons at various passes of the Great Wall, mobilized Japanese troops stationed in the three provinces of Huan, Ji, and Hei on the 21st of last month and moved them to Suizhong in western Liaoning for concentration. The Japanese troops concentrated in Suizhong moved to Qian'an on the 30th. After all disembarking, they marched on foot to Jiumenkou, joining forces with the "Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army" of Li Jichun, organized by puppet troops. On the afternoon of the 30th, several dozen enemy scouts and reconnaissance cavalry were discovered at Xiangshui, Jiumenkou, by our defending Wang Brigade [illegible] Regiment. Both sides exchanged fire with rifles. At 6:00 a.m. on the 31st, more than 300 Japanese troops suddenly launched an attack on us, and more than 20 new-style armored vehicles advanced fiercely towards Shahe. Due to our weak forces, we voluntarily withdrew to [illegible]. After suddenly crossing Shahezai at 11:00 a.m. on the 31st, the enemy increased its main force, totaling about 6,000 troops, taking a large encirclement formation against our Shimenzhai. More than 20 enemy aircraft also provided cover for explosions at 4:00 p.m. Our army stood firm. In the evening, the enemy changed to using artillery to bombard fiercely, turning the east of the Shi River line into a red glow. The battle was even more intense than the battle of Shanhaiguan.

(Fierce Day-Long Battle) At 11:00 p.m. on the 31st, our army launched a counterattack on Shahezai, but failed. At dawn yesterday (the 1st), a unit of our army concentrated in the Liangjiashan area. At 10:00 a.m., the enemy again increased its reinforcements from Jiumenkou and launched another fierce attack on our Shimenzhai. [Illegible] Army Commander Yao Dongfan personally supervised the battle in a certain area. Battles also broke out on the east bank of the Shi River at 4:00 p.m. More than a dozen enemy aircraft flew to Shimenzhai, Shihetao, Liangjiashan, and other places to bomb. Infantry and cavalry on the front also launched a joint fierce attack. Our army, based on the two highlands northwest and southwest of Shimenzhai, gave a head-on blow. The situation was very tense, with casualties on both sides reaching more than 1,000. Currently, our army in the Shahezai area has established new contact with follow-up troops, and is firmly defending Shimenzhai while bravely resisting. At 10:15 yesterday morning, when the No. 102 express train on the Beining Railway arrived in Ping, more than 30 wounded soldiers who had fought in Shimenzhai came with it. This reporter met a wounded soldier at the station, who said that the battle in Shimenzhai was extremely fierce last night (i.e., the night before), and the sound of gunfire was heard in Qinhuangdao, indicating a very serious situation. As of 2:00 p.m. yesterday, fierce battles were still ongoing near Shimenzhai.

(He [illegible] Shang Meeting) Army Commander He Guizhen of the [illegible] Army received a report of the outbreak of fighting in Shimenzhai on the afternoon of the [31st] and immediately went to the military branch to meet with He Yingqin to ask for instructions. He then left Ping on a special train at 0:50 a.m. on the 1st and arrived at [illegible] County at 10:00 a.m., intending to personally go to a certain area in the front to supervise the troops. Commander Shang Zhen of the [illegible] Army Corps also arrived at a certain area from the Lengkou front line on the evening of the 31st due to the outbreak of major battles in Shimenzhai, and met with He Zhuguo, Gao Guizhen, and others. He Guozhen sent two telegrams to Ping on the 1st, reporting the battle situation on the front. Telegram 1: (1) The enemy attacking our Shimenzhai is indeed more than 4,000 Japanese troops, the vanguard of which is 2,000 puppet troops under Li Jichun, with more than 20 tanks. Since noon yesterday (the 31st), they have repeatedly launched fierce attacks on our positions, all of which have been bravely repelled by our army. However, the enemy is extremely tenacious, and is still fighting fiercely when the telegram was sent. (2) 24 enemy aircraft have been wantonly bombing our positions in the Shimenzhai area from 8:00 a.m. to 4:00 p.m. yesterday (the 31st), causing many casualties to our army. However, the enemy has also suffered many casualties as they have been repeatedly repelled by us. (3) The attacking enemy is all wearing yellow wool uniforms, red-rimmed hats, and planting the Qing Tian Bai Ri flag, clearly a mixed force of Japanese and puppet troops, but when questioning the Japanese side, they evade responsibility by claiming that they are the "National Salvation Anti-Japanese Army." Telegram 2: At 6:00 a.m. on the morning of the 31st, about 200 enemies of the combined Japanese-puppet infantry, artillery, and air forces pressed on our sentries at Xiangshui. At 7:00 a.m., about 2,000 enemy reinforcements began a fierce attack on our Shahezai garrison. After fierce fighting between the two sides until 10:00 a.m., our army, under pressure from the superior enemy, withdrew to the [illegible] area. Fierce battles were still ongoing at noon on the 31st.

(Enemy Bombs Qinhuangdao) According to transportation circles, the battle situation in Shimenzhai was extremely fierce both the day before yesterday and yesterday. The armored train of the enemy army stationed in Shanhaiguan opened fire to show off its power at Shihe yesterday morning, and the sound of heavy artillery was also heard in Qinhuangdao. At 10:20 a.m., three enemy aircraft circled from Haiyangzhen to Qinhuangdao and dropped bombs. Our communication facilities were thus disrupted. Four enemy warships sailed into Qinhuangdao from Xie Liang Kou at 7:00 a.m. yesterday. Motor vehicles on the Beining Railway continued to depart yesterday morning. After 2:00 p.m. yesterday, details are unknown due to telephone disruptions in Qinhuangdao. (April 2nd)

Naval Headquarters from Qingdao Moved 78

Japanese Warships Being Redeployed Along the North China Coast

Shen Honglie Summoned to Nanjing by Telegram from Chiang Kai-shek

Jinan Dispatch: Japanese warships along the North China coast, belonging to the Second Overseas Dispatch Fleet, have their headquarters traditionally located in Qingdao. The commander, Tsuda, is stationed in Qingdao. Originally, the fleet consisted of three small destroyers and four cruisers, patrolling Qingdao, Yantai, Longkou, Dagu, Qinhuangdao, Lushun, and other ports. After the Rehe Incident, four additional destroyers were suddenly added, which already attracted considerable attention. Recently, the headquarters suddenly moved from Qingdao to Lushun. The flagship Hirado, carrying Commander Tsuda, left Qingdao for Lushun today (the 2nd). Tsuda himself is scheduled to travel by destroyer from Qingdao to Lushun on the 4th. While the intent of this move is unknown, it is certain that Lushun is a key Japanese port, and the relocation of the fleet headquarters there has military implications. According to a telegram from an unspecified source today, the disposition of Japanese warships is as follows: two new warships have arrived in Qingdao from Yantai; the Izumo and Tokiwa (old cruiser) are stationed in Yantai, Longkou, and Weihai; the Wakamiya seaplane tender/oiler and the Tama cruiser, along with one destroyer, are stationed in Qinhuangdao; and four destroyers and the flagship Hirado are stationed in Lushun. Our country's naval commander in Qingdao, Shen Honglie, received a telegram from Chairman Chiang Kai-shek yesterday summoning him to Nanjing. This morning (the 2nd) at 7:40 a.m., Shen arrived in Jinan. Han Fuju, Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, met with Shen at the Jiaoji Hotel to discuss matters related to the joint defense of the province's coast and land. According to Shen, his trip to Nanjing will involve separate meetings with Chiang Kai-shek and Wang Jingwei to report on the province's coastal defense and Qingdao's municipal affairs, as well as to seek instructions on everything. He expects to return in about four or five days. Shen then changed to the Jinpu Railway train heading south. (2nd)

Zhang Ji Discusses Fundamental National Salvation Policies 79

Armed Resistance and Economic Severance as Key Strategies for Resisting Aggression

Unity of the People Requires Eradication of Bureaucratic and Warlord Politics

Beijing Dispatch: Zhang Ji, Chairman of the Central North China Office, returned to Beijing from Xinxiang the morning before yesterday (the 3rd) at 8:00 a.m. Yesterday, a reporter from the Nichinichi Shimbun visited Zhang at his residence to inquire about the recent situation in North China and the fundamental policies for national salvation. He was received and gave a detailed account. The most important points are summarized below: Zhang said that the invading Japanese army is currently advancing from western Rehe towards the eastern border of Chahar, intending to gradually encroach upon the key areas of Chahar and Suiyuan in Inner Mongolia, bringing all the territory outside the Great Wall under its control, and then looking southward towards Tianjin and Beijing, invading the interior. Their plan is cunning and their intention is malicious. Although we have strengthened defenses in eastern Chahar, the future depends on the determination of the frontline soldiers and the entire nation to resist unanimously. According to news he has received, there have been no major battles at the passes along the Great Wall recently. Any contacts are merely attempts by the Japanese army to restrain our rear, as their primary objective is currently Chahar and Suiyuan.

Whether or not the North China Office will be relocated has not yet been concretely decided. His intention in establishing this office was to fulfill a fundamentally important mission, but the effectiveness depends on whether it has the power to execute its duties. If it can fulfill its tasks and avoid any difficulties, the office could be relocated from Xinxiang to Baoding, or even to the front lines. However, if relocation fails to resolve difficulties and produce results, it would be futile. As the national crisis is severe, the military, especially the North China military, should unanimously go to the front lines to kill the enemy and defend the country. But what if some soldiers are unwilling to go to the front lines? Furthermore, it is urgent for the people to organize themselves and use self-defense forces to resist the enemy. But what if local soldiers, fearing that the people's self-defense organizations might turn against them, forbid them from self-defense? Moreover, boycotting enemy goods is one way to economically restrain the enemy, but what if warlords and bureaucrats protect enemy goods and suppress the people's boycott movement? These are all important questions that deserve attention.

Regarding the way to save the nation and resist aggression, two things are most necessary and effective: (1) armed resistance and (2) economic severance. If military force and economic measures are pursued in parallel, they will certainly yield considerable results. This can be asserted with certainty. The enemy's aggression against our country also involves military force and economic measures. Japan's occupation of the Three Eastern Provinces and Rehe involved the use of cannons and machine guns to kill our people—military aggression. The dumping policy of enemy goods floods China, leaving no room for the development of domestic goods—economic aggression. To prescribe the right medicine for the ailment, national salvation and resisting aggression require only armed resistance and economic severance. However, the implementation of these requires, on one hand, that the military and the people unite and fight the enemy, and on the other hand, that the government and the people communicate as one to boycott enemy goods. To ensure smooth progress without difficulties, it is first necessary to eliminate bureaucratic and warlord politics. Otherwise, bureaucratic corruption and abuse of power will obstruct the boycott of enemy goods, and warlords will maintain their armies for self-defense, refusing to go to the front lines to resist the enemy and even preventing the people from defending themselves, all of which will affect national salvation and resisting aggression. He will soon present these matters to the central government, which should promptly discuss them. Conversely, empty talk of saving the nation without addressing the fundamentals will achieve nothing. In the four northeastern provinces, there are over three million people, including 540,000 able-bodied men. It is clear that there are many able-bodied men nationwide who can take up arms to defend the country, but they are not yet united.

Regarding the opening of political power, his intention is that political power should be exercised freely throughout the country. Currently, our country does not lack political power, but the inability of political power to flow freely is a major problem. If political power is handed over to those who can exercise it to achieve national salvation, then opening it up is acceptable. But if it is only nominal and does not help in reality, then opening up is the same as not opening up. He recalled that during the European War in 1914, when he traveled to France and Germany, France, with a population of 50 million, had over two million dead and wounded, but the people continued to go to the battlefield. Germany, with a population of 70 million, had about three million dead and wounded, but the people also continued to fight on the battlefield. Although our national crisis is severe, how many have died and been wounded? This shows the people's concept of national crisis. He recalled that in 1920 in Berlin, Germany, while staying at a hotel, he had to obtain meal tickets from the government to purchase food, demonstrating such centralized control of food supplies. Furthermore, the Rhine River was guarded by troops from various countries, but German children still traveled back and forth on the river in small boats, singing the national anthem. If a foreign soldier, drunk and walking on the road, bumped into a German, the German would slap him in the face and knock him down. The middle of the road was full of foreign soldiers, but several Germans would walk hand in hand in the middle of the road, singing German songs, and the foreign soldiers could do nothing. Compared to our country, what is the level of patriotism in Germany? In short, our revolution has not yet succeeded, and all comrades must work together and strive forward to save the nation." (Nichinichi Shimbun)

Songjiang

Monk Masterminds Robbery Case 80

The home of Ye Zhizhong of the Ye family in Heiqiao, Songjiang was robbed in broad daylight. Two robbers, Zhang Fuxing and Yang Zhengming, were apprehended in a car on the same day, and stolen goods worth 370 yuan were seized. The case has been reported. It is now known that Zhang Fuxing is a monk named Long Wu in disguise, who previously served as a guest monk at the Xilin Temple in the city. He regularly associated with retired soldiers, privately traded opium, had illicit relations with women, and engaged in illegal activities such as salt smuggling. After the abbot heard rumors of these activities, he was expelled in mid-January and went wandering. The Ye family robbery was planned after the monk performed Buddhist services at the Ye residence and became familiar with its contents. He recently learned that the Ye family had sold unpolished rice for 600 yuan, and then contacted the robbers to carry out the robbery. A monk committing robbery should serve as a warning to superstitious families.

Robbery and Assault at Nianwujiadai 81

On the evening of the 2nd, around 1 a.m., more than ten bandits armed with two guns broke into the home of He, a farmer from Nianwujiadai, south of Xiuye Bridge in the western suburbs, and began ransacking the house. When a neighbor, Ma Ahu, saw this, he shouted loudly to catch the thieves. The bandit on guard struck Ma's right leg with an iron ruler, causing him to fall in extreme pain. The gang then robbed Ma Ahu's daughter-in-law, Xiu Juan, of her earrings and two to three hundred yuan in cash, and fled with a shout. Ma Ahu's leg bone was broken by the blow, and he is currently receiving medical treatment for the injury.

Suzhou

Parricide Executed by Hanging 82

Sun Liansheng, a native of Nantong, was 30 years old. In 1930, he and his adoptive father, Sun Laowu, lived on Jiangwan Road in Shanghai. Because Liansheng idled away his days, Laowu scolded him. On the night of July 27th of that year, he colluded with his fellow villagers Ji Shuangquan, Qiu Shuntao, and Qiu Lansheng to drag Laowu from his bed and kill him. After the case was discovered, the Shanghai court sentenced him to death. He appealed to the Jiangsu High Court and the Supreme Court, both of which upheld the death sentence. Yesterday (the 4th), the High Court Prosecutor's Office received a telegram from the Ministry of Judicial Administration ordering the execution of Liansheng by hanging at the Third Branch Prison execution grounds on Siqian Street.

Three Legal Associations Strive for Repayment of Grain Loan 83

Regarding the issue of the Suzhou Finance Department's long-standing pre-borrowing of winter grain, the gentry of Wu County telegraphed the Ministry of Finance, requesting that the province be ordered to repay the loan to alleviate the suffering of the people of Suzhou. The Ministry of Finance approved the request and ordered the province to repay. However, the provincial government, citing the exhaustion of the provincial treasury, decided to postpone repayment for another year and reported this to the Ministry of Finance. The three legal associations of agriculture, commerce, and education in Suzhou, believing that the Suzhou provincial authorities were violating the Ministry's order and disregarding the people's hardships, jointly submitted a petition to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance yesterday (the 4th), requesting that the Suzhou provincial government's report be rejected and that the Suzhou provincial government be ordered to repay the loan as soon as possible to uphold the laws of the central government and alleviate the people's suffering.

Wuxi

Call for Taxation of Oil Refining 84

The self-refining kerosene industry in Wuxi is an emerging enterprise. In the summer of last year, there were only one or two factories, which, with simple equipment, were highly profitable. As a result, many people imitated them. Within half a year, the number of factories rose to more than 120. Neighboring counties such as Suzhou, Changzhou, Changshu, and Jiangyin also saw factories spring up like bamboo shoots after rain. As a result, the raw material for refining kerosene, salao oil, could not meet the demand, and the price soared to over 120 yuan per ton. Eventually, with the dumping of foreign oil and falling oil prices, the self-refining oil industry declined. Many factories closed down. Currently, there are fewer than ten factories operating normally. The Jiangsu Finance Department, seeing that the flourishing self-refining kerosene industry in various counties in the province was hindering national tax revenue, specially appointed Ding Naicheng as the Director of the Jiangsu Province Oil Refining Business Tax Collection Bureau. According to the fourth provision of the Business Tax Law, a tax of 10% is levied on net income. Director Ding, upon receiving the order, established offices in Wuxi, Suzhou, Changzhou, Jiangyin, and Changshu. Because Wuxi was the earliest and had the most factories, it was decided to start with Wuxi. A new method was also devised, stipulating that a tax of one yuan was levied for each tin of refined oil, and contacts were made with the factories separately. The factories argued that costs were high, sales were sluggish, and there was no net income to speak of, but the bureau suddenly levied one yuan, with no basis for doing so. Therefore, they strongly opposed it. Yesterday, they sent a letter to the Chamber of Commerce, requesting that it be forwarded to the Provincial Department and the Ministry of Finance and Industry, asking for relief to alleviate the hardships of businesses.

Over a Thousand Children Enthusiastically Participated

Shouldering Significant Responsibilities for the Future

April 4th is our country's National Children's Day. Yesterday was the third annual celebration. The Shanghai Municipal Children's Day Celebration Preparatory Committee held a memorial meeting at the Penglai Grand Theater in the city yesterday morning at 8:45 a.m. Details are as follows:

During this time of great national crisis, the significance is even more apparent. The well-being of the nation and its people depends entirely on the quality of education. If children receive good education from a young age, they will surely become good citizens when they grow up. The foundation of the nation is built upon the children, and the future of the new China relies entirely on the efforts of all the young brothers and sisters present here. Whether or not they succeed depends entirely on their efforts. The young brothers and sisters should bear full responsibility, so that in ten, twenty, or thirty years, we can surely become a very strong country.

(Director Pan's Address) Education Bureau Chief Pan Gongzhan said in his speech: "Today we commemorate Children's Day to save the country and the nation. This is your future hope and also your responsibility. We are happily here today, but you must think about the compatriots in the Three Northeastern Provinces, who are almost like slaves to a foreign power, and whose basic needs for food, clothing, shelter, and transportation are hardly met. There is a world of difference between them and you. How can we make them live like us? Simply put, it all depends on you children: (1) to cultivate yourselves and (2) to bear the great responsibility of saving the nation."

Statement by Mr. Backes, Representative of United Aviation Corporation 97

Acquisition of China Aviation Stock

Dedicated to Commercial Aviation

No Government Affiliation

Mainland newspapers report that since United Aviation Corporation acquired 41% of the stock of China Aviation Corporation, well-informed sources in this port have generally expected great development in China's domestic aviation industry. However, when representatives from United Aviation Corporation, including Mr. Backes, were questioned yesterday about a preliminary expansion plan, they declined to comment. Mr. Backes did acknowledge that one of the company's primary objectives is to establish a trans-Pacific air route. However, he noted that there are still many technical and other difficulties that need to be resolved before this can be achieved in the short term. For example, establishing such a route would require the cooperation of Japan or Soviet Russia, but the United States has not yet recognized Soviet Russia. Furthermore, no existing aircraft can reliably operate regular flights across the Pacific. Mr. Backes arrived in Shanghai a month ago, stayed for a few days, and then went to Guangzhou and Hong Kong. He has now returned to Shanghai from the South for another short stay. Recently, there have been widespread rumors that United Aviation Corporation's involvement in the Far East is related to the U.S. government, as the United States supposedly wants to establish aviation bases in the Pacific in preparation for any potential contingencies in U.S.-Japan relations. However, when Mr. Backes was questioned about this yesterday, he firmly denied it, stating that United Aviation Corporation is a strictly non-governmental enterprise dedicated to commercial air transport. The only relationship it has with the government is through large-scale postal service contracts. The company currently operates air routes from the United States to Central America, then along the South American coast, eastward to the capital of Argentina and westward to the capital of Chile, handling passenger and mail transport and accelerating flights. This also allows the flight crews to become familiar with the sky and ground conditions of the areas they pass through. In particular, familiarity with the Panama Canal Zone is of great military importance to the United States, because in the event of war, it would be of great value to the government. However, this is only an incidental effect of United Aviation's system, and its primary purpose is transport. Regarding the promotion of aviation in China, he is not yet prepared to release concrete plans. Currently, China Aviation Corporation operates three routes: Shanghai-Hankou, Hankou-Chongqing, and Shanghai-Beiping. The Shanghai-Guangzhou route may also be opened soon. In addition, Mr. Backes spoke at length about the future of aviation, saying that its progress is very rapid, and it is almost impossible to predict today what is possible and impossible tomorrow. United Aviation Corporation is widely regarded as the largest airline in the United States, and its involvement in the Far East is a very important move. Currently, its only competitor in China is Germany's Lufthansa.

Boundless Anger Looking South at Our Nation

While Breath Remains, How Dare I Live in Ease

According to the Nichinichi Shimbun, General Ma Zhanshan, four months after retreating to Russia, recently wired Wu Tiecheng, the mayor of this city, from Russia, stating that he will be returning to China via Europe. He first dispatched his secretary, Du Xinwu, to Shanghai to deliver a personal letter to important figures. Mr. Du, accompanied by Wu Huanzhang, General Ma's representative, visited Mayor Wu yesterday morning to report. According to Mr. Du's statement to a Nichinichi Shimbun reporter, Chairman Ma, along with Generals Su Bingwen, Li Du, and Wang Delin, departed from Moscow and plan to stay briefly in Germany to study the situation there. If they do not go through Germany, they may return via the Mediterranean Sea. The original text of General Ma's letter to Mayor Wu is excerpted below: "Tiecheng, my esteemed brother: In the past, Zhanshan followed the orders of the central government, encouraged the military and civilians, and fought fiercely with the Japanese invaders. He believed that mutual support among the armies and quick battles were crucial strategies. Therefore, in November of last year, he led a contingent of troops to Zhalantun and Hailar to discuss military matters with Commander Su Bingwen and Brigade Commander Zhang Dianjiu. Unexpectedly, the plan failed, and they were trapped in dire straits. Subsequently, due to the sudden retreat of the army, they had no choice but to retreat into the Soviet Union together. However, upon retreating, he sent personnel to order the troops near Haiman to temporarily gather in separate groups towards Kailu and Zhanyu areas on the Rehe border. For the past three months, every time I remember the enemy invaders, I feel boundless anger looking south at our nation. While breath remains, how dare I live in ease? I am now returning to China via Europe and the West. The troops returning to China via Xinjiang are under the command of the responsible officers. The civilians, women, and children returning to China via Vladivostok are being properly cared for by Hulun County Magistrate Zhan Zhenhuan and Secretary Du Xinwu. There is a date for returning to the country, and I will report the details in person. Respectfully awaiting your clear instructions, I humbly send this message and respectfully wish you peace. Sincerely, Ma Zhanshan, Chairman of the Heilongjiang Provincial Government."

Resolved to Form a Committee to Oppose to the Death

Many important proposals were resolved, the main points of which are as follows: (1) China's fishing industry has declined to the extreme, and all fishermen and merchants find it difficult to bear any expenses. They unanimously insist on opposing the fisheries construction fee that will be levied soon. (2) A temporary "Jiangsu and Zhejiang Fishermen and Merchants Committee to Deny the Collection of Fisheries Construction Fee" will be organized to oppose it to the death, without stopping until the goal is achieved. (3) An appeal delegation will be organized, a declaration will be issued, and a division of labor will be determined. (4) Letters will be sent to various fish markets, requesting that they follow the letter of February 8th and "rather cease operations than withhold the construction fee on behalf of the government." After the proposals were discussed, the meeting adjourned.

The Bureau of Public Works Investigation Report on the Zhengtai Rubber Factory Incident 109

The Poor Equipment of Various Rubber Factories

Measures to be Taken to Prevent Danger

On February 21st of this year, an explosion occurred at the Zhengtai Rubber Factory on Tangshan Road. The Bureau of Public Works ordered the relevant departments to investigate and report. The report was submitted to the board of directors on March 15th and has now been delivered to the Security Committee for detailed review in order to propose solutions. The main points of the report are recorded below:

Possible Causes of the Explosion 110

The head of the Fire Department believes that the explosion and fire were both caused by a vulcanizer. The lid of the furnace was blown forty feet away. The explosion of the furnace was due to an electrical spark igniting a mixture of air and gasoline. The cause of the spark is unknown. The combustion of this mixed gas requires a temperature of 390 degrees Celsius. According to the statements of two witnesses, they first saw an electrical spark, and then the entire room was filled with flames. If the gasoline gas in the room reaches a certain concentration, it can be ignited by a spark. But in this case, the rupture of the furnace should be later. In short, whether the explosion originated inside or outside the furnace, preventive measures must be taken.

Research on the Properties of Gasoline 111

The main danger of a rubber factory lies in the use of gasoline as a solvent. Commercially used gasoline contains about 23% light carbon compounds and can volatilize at 0 degrees Celsius. The factory usually has a temperature of 30 degrees, so the amount of volatilization is naturally higher. According to the test of the Health Department, the gasoline commonly used in Shanghai begins to boil at about 43 degrees, but combustion requires a temperature of 390 degrees. Electrical sparks can provide this high temperature. The combustion composition of gasoline needs to reach 1.6% to 5.3% in the air. If this degree has been reached, it is inevitable to explode when encountering sparks, or sparks from the collision of clocks and instruments, or uncovered lamps and candles.

Equipment Conditions of Various Rubber Factories 112

According to the investigation, there are 27 rubber factories in the Public Concession, employing about 3,000 workers. In 1927, there was only one, and the rest were opened in the last five years. Among these 27, 18 had submitted construction plans to the Public Works Department, 7 were converted from Chinese-style houses, and unapproved additions that could cause danger were found in 10. Those converted from thin Chinese-style houses have had their internal partitions removed, and the upper and lower floors are still connected by steep stairs, usually only two. Heavy machinery is installed downstairs, and many female workers work upstairs. Those with only one floor have workers working in the boiler room. The light is insufficient, and lights must be lit during the day, and the temperature inside the room is particularly high with few windows. Gasoline gas is heavier than air, and none of the rubber factories have ground ventilation equipment. In addition, there are many concerns about the installation of electrical appliances, the storage and use of gasoline, and other dangers to the life and health of workers.

Measures to be Taken to Prevent Danger (A) Regarding Building Construction: 113

1. Before applying for a building permit for a rubber factory, the site should be approved in advance.

2. The factory building must be specially constructed and fireproof. The gasification work room must be appropriately isolated.

3. The room where most workers work shall not be located above a room where an explosion is possible.

4. Existing factories that are unsuitable must be immediately renovated or moved.

**(B) Regarding Electrical Equipment:**

1. All generators, switches, fuses, lamp holders, and other electrical equipment must have special installations where there is gasoline gas.

2. The wiring must be arranged safely.

**(C) Regarding Preventing the Danger of Gasification:**

1. This work room must be isolated.

2. Before the rubber overshoes enter the vulcanizer, they should be placed in a ventilated drying room so that the gasoline gas in them can be dissipated.

3. Do not allow iron to strike or grind, so as not to catch fire.

4. The belts on the axles must be "endless" to avoid static electricity. The joints of the belts must be glued together and not connected with metal. The inside of the belt should be coated with pencil lead and rosin.

5. Fresh air should be introduced from the high part of the room, and unclean air should be discharged from the ground by mechanical means. The generator that transports air should be located outside the room, and the electric fan should also be located outside or isolated. The discharged gas should be released to a height considerably above the roof.

6. The gasoline used by workers should be placed in closable containers. Glass bottles must not be used. (Because pouring gasoline from glass bottles can generate electricity.)

7. Wiping rags should be placed in a covered iron box and placed outside the room.

8. The storage of large amounts of gasoline should be handled according to regulations. Those placed outside are only allowed to be sufficient for one day's use. When not needed, they should be placed in a special storage place outside the work room.

Other Dangers to be Noted 114

In addition to the danger of explosion, when rolling crude rubber, it is necessary to add powders of lead and other compounds, which is harmful to the health of workers when inhaled. The inhalation of gasoline gas is also harmful and must have adequate ventilation equipment. Workers should wash their hands before meals. Eating is not allowed in any room where aluminum gasification work is done. Also, the grinding room is full of dust, which can also explode. Electrical equipment in it should also be paid attention to in the same way. In short, the factory building must be legal, all places must be clean, objects must not be discarded randomly, the worker exit must be sufficient and not blocked, and the toilet waste must have a suitable location. All of these must be inspected at any time before safety can be expected.

The Ministry of Industry Replied to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce that Foreign Merchants Have No Patent Rights in China 115

There is No Restriction on Imitating Foreign Goods

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from a Chinese factory stating that it intended to imitate foreign goods, with the same style and raw materials, and asked whether it was possible to imitate them. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce found that the "Provisional Regulations on Encouraging Industrial Technology" promulgated by the government order on September 30, 1932, stipulated that the right to enjoy patent rights for industrial articles or methods first invented is limited to citizens of the Republic of China. Foreign merchants with patented articles in their home country cannot prohibit Chinese merchants from imitating them within the territory of China. It specially requested the Ministry of Industry for an explanation. The Ministry of Industry replied: "I have received your telegram. As the Chinese Patent Law has not yet been formulated and promulgated, foreign merchants with patented articles in their home country naturally cannot enjoy patent rights within China. You should immediately inform them of this reply."

The Municipal Government Issued a Notice Prohibiting Foremen from Deducting Wages of Dock Workers 117

No Additional Exploitation to Eliminate Disputes

Dock workers in this city are suffering from extreme hardship due to the exploitation and deduction of wages by foremen. The dock affairs office specifically requested the municipal government to issue a notice to prohibit such practices in order to maintain the livelihood of the workers. The municipal government issued the following notice yesterday: "Notice is hereby given that, according to the report submitted by Zhang Jianbai, the standing commissioner of the Shanghai Dock Affairs Office, since the establishment of this office, there have been many cases reported to the office by dock workers regarding exploitation and deduction of wages by foremen. The reason for this is that during the national crisis, commerce has declined, and the loading and unloading of goods has decreased daily. Taking advantage of this decrease in goods and the surplus of workers, the foremen have not hesitated to hoard and deduct wages in order to maintain their previous income. The livelihood of workers is the most difficult for dock workers. In the past, when goods were crowded, the blood and sweat they earned every day were not enough to provide a meal. At a time when the national crisis is becoming increasingly urgent and the people's livelihood is becoming more difficult, and when they are subjected to additional exploitation by foremen, their lives are even more unbearable. Their repeated reports to this office are a kind of urgent appeal by the workers themselves in a state of hunger and cold, and are not aimed at any hostility or difficulty towards the foremen. There are more than 80,000 dock workers. If the foremen are allowed to oppress and exploit them for a long time, the lives of the workers will be further plunged into a desperate situation. If this causes disputes and affects social security, it will be a matter of no small importance. Therefore, it is requested that your government issue a notice to all docks to strictly prohibit foremen from exploiting workers and deducting wages in order to maintain the lives of the workers and the security of this city, which is truly a public convenience. According to this, the livelihood of dock workers is the most difficult, which is the truth. If the foremen exploit and deduct wages, it is obviously inappropriate. According to the report, a notice must be issued urgently, ordering all dock foremen in the city to abide by it together. They must not exploit workers or deduct wages, so as to eliminate disputes. If anyone dares to violate this order, they will be severely punished according to the law. Wu Tiecheng, Mayor."

British Soldiers Surveying Maps Outside the Concession 119

Police Interference and Prevention

Lei Zaixi, the police chief of the Hejiajiao Police Station, Second Branch of the Sixth District of Xujiahui in western Shanghai, was patrolling Zhongshan Road yesterday morning around 10:00 AM when he spotted more than ten British soldiers in six cars parked by the roadside at the intersection of Hongqiao Road and Zhongshan Road. The soldiers were surveying maps. Chief Lei, considering that the area belonged to the Chinese territory and involved sovereignty, advised them to stop working. The soldiers refused. Therefore, he took the driver, Cheng Afu, to the station. After a brief interrogation by Station Chief Wu, Cheng Afu confessed that he was 52 years old, a native of Shanghai, residing at No. 9 Metcalfe Road, and worked as a driver inside the British barracks on Daxi Road. The car number was 1448. At 8:30 AM this morning, he drove the car from the British military commander's house on the 13th floor to the British barracks at No. 63 Daxi Road, where more than ten soldiers boarded six cars and got off at the intersection of Zhongshan Road and Hongqiao Road to draw maps. Station Chief Wu, based on the confession, ordered Cheng Afu to be temporarily detained pending further investigation.

Youth Petitions to Join the Army and Kill the Enemy 121

Although There Are Some Typos in the Petition, the Handwriting Is Quite Elegant

Unable to Find a Friend After Crossing the Huangpu River, He Suddenly Wants to Commit Suicide

丨Now Under the Relief Efforts of the Second Section of the Public Security Bureau丨

Around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, a young man wearing a student uniform of free cloth boarded a rowing boat at the Muddy Ferry Pier in Pudong to cross the Huangpu River. After the boat left the dock, the young man suddenly wanted to commit suicide by jumping into the river. Fortunately, the boatman noticed and stopped him before he went into the water. The boat then returned to Pudong, and the boatman handed him over to the police officer on duty to be taken to the Third District. After questioning by the district chief, the young man stated that his name was Jin Bo, 18 years old, from Shaoxing, residing in front of the Old Yue Temple in the city of his hometown. He had been studying in a private school in the city. His father's name was Xi En, 48 years old, working as a partner in a general merchandise store. His mother was 37 years old. Recently, his parents were secretly harmed by foreigners and fled, their whereabouts unknown. He had no siblings at home, and the house was rented, so it was difficult for him to stay alone. Therefore, he left home alone and came to Shanghai after much wandering. On the way, he heard that various counties were recruiting soldiers. He felt that the country was in danger and that it was time for him to join the army and serve the country. Therefore, he decided to register for military service in Shanghai County. However, after arriving in Shanghai for three days, his travel expenses were exhausted. He then remembered that his friend Chen Tianxi lived in Pudong, so he came to Pudong today to borrow a few silver dollars from Chen for pocket money. Unexpectedly, he searched everywhere but could not find him, and it was difficult to live if he went back, so he had the idea of ​​ending his life. The district chief also found a written petition to join the army on his person, which he had written himself. Although there were typos and incomprehensible sentences, the handwriting was quite elegant (the original text is recorded later). The district chief thought his ambition was commendable, so he ordered a document to be prepared and sent to the Second Section of the General Bureau for relief (Petition to Join the Army). Petition for Military Service: China, since the January 28th Shanghai Incident, the enemy has invaded our territory, and the hatred has not ceased. They occupy our territory, take one step further, and are insatiable. Our army is numerous, but its strength is unequal to the enemy because its guns are not as good as the enemy's. Therefore, it is difficult to win. As a result, the violent Japanese bully us, Rehe has fallen, and North China is shaken. The evil forces are gradually endangering us. The hatred between us and Japan is deeply etched in our hearts. How can we, the youth, bear to sit and watch our country perish? We should fight to the death against the enemy. The people have long wanted to resist the enemy, but there is no way to volunteer. Now that we know that various provinces and counties are recruiting new soldiers, we cannot help but feel a surge of murderous intent. Therefore, we eagerly come to join the army and obey training, so that we can kill the enemy and fulfill our duty. We humbly ask the authorities to accept us, and we will be eternally grateful. Respectfully presented to the Shanghai County Magistrate (omitted below).

Bomb Explodes on Haichang Road, Injuring Four 122

Injured and Collapsed on the Ground, Flesh and Blood Flying

Shen Hongbin Has Shrapnel Embedded in His Neck

Yesterday afternoon at 3:30 PM, at No. 3 Pede North Lane, west of Yaojia Stone Bridge on Haichang Road in Zhabei, Shen Guigen (45 years old), a native of Taizhou who works as an opera singer, had a son named Hongbao, 24 years old, who earns a living by pulling a rickshaw. In the afternoon, he returned from outside and picked up a bomb that looked like an olive but was larger. Hongbao did not know what it was and took it to the front building. He first lit it with a match, but nothing happened. Then he lit it with an oil lamp. Unexpectedly, the bomb exploded from the heat. With a loud bang, Hongbao was injured and collapsed on the ground. Shrapnel was shot into his neck and legs. Hongbao's mother, Madam Shen (50 years old), was also hit in the face by shrapnel. His wife (20 years old) was injured in the right temple. A nine-year-old girl named Caixi, who lived upstairs in the same building and had the surname Hu, was injured in the top of her head. All of them had flesh and blood flying everywhere. The floor, the bed, and the tables and chairs were stained red. Later, they were sent to Pushan Hospital for treatment. The alley was covered in bloodstains, which was a terrible sight. Ma Zhenwu, the police officer on duty at Post No. 12 of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau, also rushed to the scene after hearing the explosion. After inspecting the scene, he immediately reported to the Fourth District. Patrol officers and police chiefs were sent to investigate and confirm the facts. They reported back to District Chief Lai. Among the four injured, except for Hongbao, his mother, wife, and the nine-year-old girl upstairs had shrapnel removed by doctors, applied with good medicine, and bandaged up. However, Hongbao's injuries were more serious. Shrapnel was embedded deep in his neck and was not easy to remove at the time. After the doctors temporarily bandaged him, they instructed him to be transferred to Baolong Hospital, saying that his life might be in danger.

Immoral Monk Arrested for Murder 123

Such a Ferocious Disciple of Buddhism

Directly Admits Guilt in Court

The monk Nengjing, originally from Xinghua, Jiangbei, is now 41 years old. A woman from his hometown named Ouyang Liu, who was widowed at the age of 29, had an affair with the monk. From then on, they became illicitly acquainted and lived together in a kitchen at No. 68 Siwen Lane, Datong Road, Xinzha. The monk, being a lustful demon, did not chant scriptures but relied on begging for alms to make a living, causing Ouyang Liu to constantly feel that her income could not meet her expenses. A worker named Fan Weisheng, who did odd jobs, often went to her house to smoke opium, and they also became illicitly acquainted. Ouyang Liu also moved Fan into her room because Nengjing would often be away for several days when he went begging for alms, making it easier for them to share a bed and talk. On August 11 of last year, Nengjing returned and saw this situation, which aroused his jealousy. He questioned the woman. The woman, caught between the two men, worked hard to mediate. Seeing Nengjing's angry expression, she lied to him, saying that Fan was only renting a bed in the room, paying two yuan a month, which was a small but helpful supplement, and that the rent was paid in advance. Even if she wanted to evict him, she would have to wait until he had lived there for a month before dismissing him. The monk was deceived by the woman's words, and his anger subsided slightly, but his resentment was still difficult to quell. At 10:00 PM on the 14th, he secretly took a cow ear-shaped knife and went home. He saw the woman lying outside the room, while Fan was sleeping inside. The monk insisted that the woman enter the room and sleep with him, but the woman refused because of the hot weather. The monk then slept alone. At 3:15 AM the next morning, he suddenly had the urge to kill. In the dim light, he approached Fan's bed. Fan was fast asleep. The monk suddenly used the sharp knife to stab Fan in a vital spot. Fan woke up from his sleep in pain and shouted loudly. The woman was also awakened and entered the room. She saw Fan lying in a pool of blood. The monk was about to stab the woman with the knife, but she shouted for help, and he abandoned the knife and fled. Fan died several hours later. The police station reported the case to the First Special District District Court. The prosecutor examined the body, ordered it to be coffined and buried, and issued an arrest warrant to apprehend the murderer and punish him according to law. After half a year, Feng Baishun, a detective from the Putuo Road Police Station, learned that the monk had recently fled back to Shanghai and was still living with the woman at No. 9 Yongan Lane, Hengtong Road, Zhabei. He rushed there at 1:30 AM yesterday and arrested them both. They were then sent to the First Special Court, where Judge Qian Wenji conducted a preliminary hearing. After the police lawyer Chen Ming presented the case, he requested that the defendant Nengjing be prosecuted for premeditated murder under Article 284 of the Criminal Code. Ouyang Liu was asked to testify about the situation at the time and to confront the defendant's testimony. Nengjing confessed, "If I didn't kill Fan, Fan would definitely gather his gang and break my arms and legs. Liu told me this, so I killed him." Liu confessed, "Fan did say this." Judge Qian then ordered Ouyang Liu to be released and the defendant to be detained for further interrogation at a later date.

Zhao Fuhai Left Fire in a Pile of Firewood

Burning More Than Twenty Thatched Houses

Because there was no fire-fighting equipment, it was allowed to burn naturally until it was extinguished the next morning. The households affected by the fire were unable to save their belongings and suffered great losses. It is said that the municipal government is now planning to ban the thatched sheds to prevent fires.

Huamin Socks Factory Asks Taxpayers' Association to Protest Police Interference in Night Work 126

Cui Zhenhua and Yu Dabao of Huamin Socks Factory on Binlang Road in western Shanghai yesterday asked the Public Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association to protest the police interference in the factory's night work and machine noise case. The original letter is recorded below: Respectfully, we rent a house at No. 1027 Binlang Road to operate a sock weaving business. Unexpectedly, yesterday we received a summons from the First Special District District Court because we had been working the machines late at night from 12:00 AM to 6:00 AM every night in March this year, disturbing the sleep of residents, and the police had filed a lawsuit for violation of regulations. Upon learning this, we were shocked. We operate a legitimate business and pay taxes according to regulations. Due to business reasons, we have to work night shifts. Now the police of the Ding Department actually consider it a violation of regulations and file a criminal lawsuit, which is tantamount to depriving merchants of their livelihoods. We are one of the taxpayers in the Concession, and your association is an organization to protect the interests of Chinese taxpayers. Therefore, we dare to send this letter requesting your association's assistance and hope that you will protest based on the following two points: (1) Has the Ding Department divided the Concession area into factory areas and residential areas? (2) Has the Bureau of Works previously had a proposal to manage factories in the Concession, and has there been any result or agreement after consultation with the Chinese authorities? (3) Does operating night shifts in factories violate the Bureau of Works' police regulations? If the Bureau of Works has not yet designated which areas are factory areas and which areas are residential areas, and operating night shifts in factories does not violate the police regulations, then we are forced to work night shifts for business needs, and the Bureau of Works has no reason to file a lawsuit for violation of regulations. Furthermore, there are many factories set up by people of any nationality in the Concession that have night shifts, and we have never heard of the Bureau of Works filing a lawsuit for violation of regulations. Moreover, if we talk about disturbing the sleep of residents, then the vibration of heavy vehicles driving at night, the noise of car horns, or any other noise is enough to disturb people's sleep, and the Ding Department will probably consider all of them to be violations of regulations. In short, this matter concerns our small interests, but if this is used as a precedent, the losses to the Chinese merchant factories that work night shifts in the future will be unimaginable. Your association has always been committed to protecting the rights of taxpayers, so we hope you will uphold justice, protest to the Bureau of Works based on reason, and request the court to explain so as to avoid innocent people being forced. Not only will we be grateful, but the impact on all factories in Shanghai will be no small matter.

Zhengxin Industrial and Commercial Directory Comes Out 131

The Zhengxin Industrial and Commercial Directory, edited by the China Zhengxin Institute, was originally scheduled to be published at the end of February. The institute then considered the end of January as the end of the business community's big closure period. The operation of going in and out, and the personnel transfer, are decided at this time. It is the most drastic period of change in the economic society. If the directory does not include this new undertaking, it will not be able to express the highest effectiveness. Therefore, the typesetting was sent to the listed industrial and commercial firms for re-examination and correction, and then sent to print. The publication date was delayed by one month, and it was released at the end of March and began to be sold on April 1. The directory is not only new in information, but also rich in content. The number of listed companies reaches more than 7,000, which is more than double that of other directories. Almost all of the important industrial and commercial firms in this city have been listed. The compilation method is also extremely meticulous. In addition to the Chinese and Western names of Chinese people being listed together, there is also a Chinese name index. Various important information is also listed in both Chinese and English, so that those who do not understand English can also use it freely, which is unique to other directories. The most powdery Hua Ying Shanghai City Atlas with street index is attached for sale, which is accurate and detailed, and convenient to review. All those engaged in the industrial and commercial community and various institutions, as long as they have a directory and a map, can know the situation of Shanghai's economic society like the back of their hand. The price is also very low compared with similar publications, 6 yuan per copy, and the monthly correction form is 1 yuan per copy per year. The Shanghai City Atlas with street index is 1.5 yuan per copy for a single purchase, and a total of 7 yuan for purchasing with the directory. The number of people who went to the institute at No. 4 Hong Kong Road to buy it in the past few days was unusually large.

丨Elementary School Student Testifies in Court丨

Guo Zhenqing, a resident of Jiangbei, at around 5 PM the day before yesterday, was picking up a piece of wood near house number 356 on Fielun Road near Yalu Road, in front of the Shen Rongji Construction Factory, intending to take it home for firewood. According to the doctor, the injuries to his abdomen and buttocks were severe, and his life was in danger. He requested that the case be postponed. According to Guo and Li's statement, the first defendant, Shen Hanshan, initiated the fight over picking up the wood, attacking her husband without regard to the circumstances, beating him to the ground with fists and feet. The second defendant, Min Amao, and others joined in the assault, and she was also knocked down and injured. Zhou Ximiao, a fifteen-year-old Ningbo child, stated that he lived on Fielun Road and was returning home from school at the time. He saw five or six people beating a man and a woman to the ground without weapons, using only their fists. The two defendants claimed that they had also been injured in the waist and face but that their injuries were minor and requested consideration. Judge Wu ordered them to be remanded in custody and that the case be reviewed after the victims had recovered from their injuries.

Suspicious Death of a Female Worker 139

丨Rumor Has It She Died Due to an Abortion丨

Gao Ruyizi, a woman from Yangzhou, was twenty-two years old and had good looks. She was not yet married. Several years ago, her fellow townsman, Sheng Chunlan (currently forty-five years old), worked as a meal provider in the Dakang Cotton Mill on Pingliang Road in East Shanghai. The woman's parents, hoping to increase their income, sent Sheng to bring her to Shanghai and recommend her for work in the factory, entrusting Sheng to take care of her. As a result, the woman's food and lodging were provided by him, and her wages were used to supplement it. For several years, they lived peacefully. Unexpectedly, ten days ago, the woman suddenly fell ill. Sheng hired a traditional Chinese medicine doctor to treat her, but it was ineffective. Three days ago, her illness worsened, and she died in the early morning at around 2 AM. According to people in the factory, Sheng had an affair with the woman, resulting in a secret pregnancy. They performed an abortion to avoid being discovered, which led to her illness and death. The Yangshupu Police Station was notified and dispatched Chinese Detective Li Dacheng to investigate. He had the body taken to the autopsy room on Fielun Road. Yesterday morning, he reported to the First Special District Court and requested Prosecutor Guo Wei, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, to examine the body. The factory's night watchman, Japanese man Kikuchi Tadao, testified that he did not personally witness the abortion, but he had heard people say that the woman had an abortion ten days ago. He believed that Sheng found medicine for her to take, and no one was called to perform surgery. Sheng Chunlan testified that the deceased lived with him. Because she had a stomach ache, he hired a doctor for her and presented a copy of the prescription. He stated that he never had physical relations with her, but he did not know if she had a relationship with anyone else. He had notified her parents, who would come to Shanghai to take care of everything. After Guo's testimony, he determined that there was not enough evidence in this case and decided to order an autopsy. The hearing was rescheduled for this Thursday.

Russian Swindler Unrepentant 141

The Russian swindler, Er Qi, is thirty-seven years old this year and lives at house number 3, Yermoni Lane, Avenue Joffre. He has committed eight crimes in the French and British concessions. He was released from prison last year. Unexpectedly, he has recently relapsed. He issued fake checks to the rubber tire store run by the Westerner Luo Linsi at number 631, Avenue Huixu, the Lasi store at number 314, Avenue Albert, and the Xina Pharmacy on Avenue Joffre, obtaining goods worth several hundred dollars. When the victims were unable to cash the checks, they realized they had been defrauded and reported to the police, who ordered the detectives to arrest him and take him to the police station. Yesterday, he was sent to the Second Special Court. The police lawyer, Yuan Jiahuang, explained the case and said that the police were investigating whether the defendant had defrauded other stores. He requested an adjournment for further questioning. The victims then complained about being defrauded. The defendant gave evasive answers. Judge Zhang Renkan ordered the defendant to post 6,000 dollars in cash and a guarantor for release pending trial.

Boy Killed by Taxi 142

Yesterday afternoon around 3 PM, a Yong'an Motor Company taxi, number 18102, was driving on Avenue de Say Zoet. At that moment, an eleven-year-old boy named Chen Ayou was playing in the road. The driver was driving too fast and knocked him down, crushing his head. A policeman at post number 200 nearby saw the incident, immediately stopped the car, and brought it to the police station. He also sent the injured boy to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Unfortunately, he died soon after due to his severe injuries. The hospital reported the incident to the police station, who transported the body to the autopsy room for examination, pending a report to the court today for examination and handling.

Zhejiang Industrial Bank Inspection Report 143

The thirty-fourth inspection report on the issuance of currency by Zhejiang Industrial Bank states: The issuance of currency by Zhejiang Industrial Bank is completely separate from its business operations, and the reserves are sufficient. On the fourth of this month, after an inspection by accountant Yan Ouke, the cash reserves accounted for over 60%, and the security reserves accounted for under 40%. All the numbers are as follows: The bank's issued currency totaled 3,528,416.50 yuan. The reserve funds included 2,400,416.50 yuan in cash and 1,128,000 yuan in security. The amount used by other banks totaled 3,230,000 yuan. The reserve funds included 1,991,000 yuan in cash and 1,239,000 yuan in security.
